			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Michelle Obama</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">

<p><b>Michelle LaVaughn Robinson Obama</b> (born January 17, 1964) is an American lawyer and writer who was <a href="/wiki/First_Lady_of_the_United_States" title="First Lady of the United States">First Lady of the United States</a> from 2009 to 2017. She is married to the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_the_United_States" title="List of Presidents of the United States">44th</a> President of the United States, <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, and is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_African-American_firsts" title="List of African-American firsts">first African-American</a> First Lady. Raised on the <a href="/wiki/South_Side,_Chicago" title="South Side, Chicago">South Side</a> of Chicago, Illinois, Obama is a graduate of <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">Princeton University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Law_School" title="Harvard Law School">Harvard Law School</a>, and spent her early legal career working at the law firm <a href="/wiki/Sidley_Austin" title="Sidley Austin">Sidley Austin</a>, where she met her husband. She subsequently worked as the Associate Dean of Student Services at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">University of Chicago</a> and the Vice President for Community and External Affairs of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Medical_Center" title="University of Chicago Medical Center">University of Chicago Medical Center</a>. Barack and Michelle married in 1992 and have two daughters.</p>
<p>Obama campaigned for her <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama_presidential_campaign,_2008" title="Barack Obama presidential campaign, 2008">husband's presidential bid</a> throughout 2007 and 2008, delivering a keynote address at the <a href="/wiki/2008_Democratic_National_Convention" title="2008 Democratic National Convention">2008 Democratic National Convention</a>. She returned to speak at the <a href="/wiki/2012_Democratic_National_Convention" title="2012 Democratic National Convention">2012 Democratic National Convention</a>, and again during the <a href="/wiki/2016_Democratic_National_Convention" title="2016 Democratic National Convention">2016 Democratic National Convention</a> in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, where she delivered a speech in support of the Democratic presidential nominee, and fellow First Lady, <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a>.</p>
<p>As First Lady, Obama became a role model for women, an advocate for poverty awareness, nutrition, physical activity and healthy eating, and a fashion icon.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Family_and_education">Family and education</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Family_of_Barack_Obama#Michelle_Robinson_Obama.27s_extended_family" title="Family of Barack Obama">Michelle Robinson Obama's extended family</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_ancestry">Early life and ancestry</span></h3>
<p>Michelle LaVaughn Robinson was born on January 17, 1964, in <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago, Illinois</a>, to Fraser Robinson III,<sup id="cite_ref-TFToMOtFL_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TFToMOtFL-3">[3]</a></sup> a city water plant employee and <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Precinct_captain" title="Precinct captain">precinct captain</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Marian_Shields_Robinson" title="Marian Shields Robinson">Marian Shields Robinson</a>, a secretary at <a href="/wiki/Spiegel_(catalog)" title="Spiegel (catalog)">Spiegel's catalog store</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-womanbehind_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-womanbehind-4">[4]</a></sup> Her mother was a full-time homemaker until Michelle entered high school.<sup id="cite_ref-PAW2009_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PAW2009-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Robinson and Shields families trace their roots to pre-<a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">Civil War</a> African Americans in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">American South</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TFToMOtFL_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TFToMOtFL-3">[3]</a></sup> On her father's side, she is descended from the <a href="/wiki/Gullah" title="Gullah">Gullah</a> people of South Carolina's <a href="/wiki/Lowcountry" class="mw-redirect" title="Lowcountry">Low Country</a> region.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Her paternal great-great grandfather, Jim Robinson, was a <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_United_States" title="Slavery in the United States">slave</a> on <a href="/wiki/Friendfield_Plantation" title="Friendfield Plantation">Friendfield Plantation</a> in <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-soil_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soil-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cabin_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cabin-8">[8]</a></sup> the state where some of her paternal family still reside.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NPR_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPR-10">[10]</a></sup> Her grandfather Fraser Robinson, Jr. built his own house in South Carolina. He and his wife LaVaughn (née Johnson) returned to the Low Country after retirement.<sup id="cite_ref-soil_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soil-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>Among her maternal ancestors was her great-great-great-grandmother, Melvinia Shields, a slave on Henry Walls Shields' 200-acre farm in <a href="/wiki/Clayton_County,_Georgia" title="Clayton County, Georgia">Clayton County, Georgia</a>. Melvinia's first son, Dolphus T. Shields, was biracial and born into slavery about 1860. Based on DNA and other evidence, in 2012 researchers said his father was likely 20-year-old Charles Marion Shields, son of her master.<sup id="cite_ref-swarns_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-swarns-11">[11]</a></sup> Melvinia did not talk to relatives about Dolphus' father.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT-maternal_ancestry_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-maternal_ancestry-12">[12]</a></sup> Dolphus Shields moved to <a href="/wiki/Birmingham,_Alabama" title="Birmingham, Alabama">Birmingham, Alabama</a> after the Civil War, and some of his children migrated to <a href="/wiki/Cleveland,_Ohio" class="mw-redirect" title="Cleveland, Ohio">Cleveland, Ohio</a> and Chicago.<sup id="cite_ref-swarns_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-swarns-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>All four of her grandparents had multiracial ancestors, reflecting the complex history of the U.S., but her extended family has said that people did not talk about the era of slavery when they were growing up.<sup id="cite_ref-swarns_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-swarns-11">[11]</a></sup> Her distant ancestry includes Irish and other European roots.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> In addition, a paternal first cousin once-removed is the African-American Jewish <a href="/wiki/Rabbi" title="Rabbi">Rabbi</a> <a href="/wiki/Capers_Funnye" title="Capers Funnye">Capers Funnye</a>, son of her grandfather's sister.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT090402_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT090402-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fwd_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fwd-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Robinson grew up in a two-story bungalow on Euclid Avenue in Chicago's <a href="/wiki/South_Shore,_Chicago" title="South Shore, Chicago">South Shore</a> <a href="/wiki/Community_areas_of_Chicago" class="mw-redirect" title="Community areas of Chicago">community area</a>. Her parents rented a small apartment on the second floor from her great-aunt, who lived downstairs.<sup id="cite_ref-womanbehind_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-womanbehind-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WaPo2009-02-01_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WaPo2009-02-01-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NY052404_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NY052404-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MOAL_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOAL-18">[18]</a></sup> She was raised in what she describes as a "conventional" home, with "the mother at home, the father works, you have dinner around the table."<sup id="cite_ref-FLIW_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLIW-19">[19]</a></sup> Her elementary school was down the street. They enjoyed playing games such as <a href="/wiki/Monopoly_(board_game)" class="mw-redirect" title="Monopoly (board game)">Monopoly</a>, reading, and frequently saw extended family on both sides.<sup id="cite_ref-MOSS_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOSS-20">[20]</a></sup> She played piano,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> learning from her great-aunt who was a piano teacher.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The Robinsons attended services at nearby South Shore United Methodist Church.<sup id="cite_ref-WaPo2009-02-01_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WaPo2009-02-01-16">[16]</a></sup> They used to vacation in a rustic cabin in <a href="/wiki/White_Cloud,_Michigan" title="White Cloud, Michigan">White Cloud, Michigan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WaPo2009-02-01_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WaPo2009-02-01-16">[16]</a></sup> She and her 21-month older brother, <a href="/wiki/Craig_Robinson_(basketball)" title="Craig Robinson (basketball)">Craig</a>, skipped the second grade.<sup id="cite_ref-womanbehind_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-womanbehind-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>Her father suffered from <a href="/wiki/Multiple_sclerosis" title="Multiple sclerosis">multiple sclerosis</a> which had a profound emotional effect on her as she was growing up. She was determined to stay out of trouble and be a good student, which was what her father wanted for her.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> By sixth grade, Michelle joined a gifted class at Bryn Mawr Elementary School (later renamed Bouchet Academy).<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> She attended <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Young_Magnet_High_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Whitney Young Magnet High School">Whitney Young High School</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-West_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-West-26">[26]</a></sup> Chicago's first <a href="/wiki/Magnet_school" title="Magnet school">magnet high school</a>, established as a selective enrollment school, where she was a classmate of <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Jackson" title="Jesse Jackson">Jesse Jackson</a>'s daughter <a href="/wiki/Santita_Jackson" title="Santita Jackson">Santita</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MOSS_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOSS-20">[20]</a></sup> The round-trip commute from the Robinsons' South Side home to the <a href="/wiki/Near_West_Side,_Chicago" title="Near West Side, Chicago">Near West Side</a>, where the school was located, took three hours.<sup id="cite_ref-tn_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tn-27">[27]</a></sup> She recalled being fearful of how others would perceive her, but disregarded any negativity around her and used it "to fuel me, to keep me going."<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> She recalled experiencing <a href="/wiki/Gender_discrimination" class="mw-redirect" title="Gender discrimination">gender discrimination</a> growing up, saying, for example, that rather than asking her for her opinion on a given subject, people commonly tended to ask what her older brother thought.<sup id="cite_ref-2015CNN_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015CNN-30">[30]</a></sup> She was on the honor roll for four years, took <a href="/wiki/Advanced_placement" class="mw-redirect" title="Advanced placement">advanced placement</a> classes, was a member of the <a href="/wiki/National_Honor_Society" title="National Honor Society">National Honor Society</a>, and served as <a href="/wiki/Student_council" title="Student council">student council</a> treasurer.<sup id="cite_ref-womanbehind_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-womanbehind-4">[4]</a></sup> She graduated in 1981 as the <a href="/wiki/Salutatorian" title="Salutatorian">salutatorian</a> of her class.<sup id="cite_ref-tn_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tn-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_early_career">Education and early career</span></h3>
<p>She was inspired to follow her brother to <a href="/wiki/Princeton_University" title="Princeton University">Princeton University</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-PAW2009_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PAW2009-5">[5]</a></sup> where he graduated in 1983,<sup id="cite_ref-Bond41_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bond41-31">[31]</a></sup> after which he went on to become a basketball coach at <a href="/wiki/Oregon_State_University" title="Oregon State University">Oregon State University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brown_University" title="Brown University">Brown University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-craig_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-craig-32">[32]</a></sup> She recalls that some of her teachers in high school tried to dissuade her from applying, that she had been told she was "setting my sights too high".<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> She believed that her brother's status as an alumnus may have helped her during the admission process,<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> but she was resolved to demonstrate her own worthiness.<sup id="cite_ref-Bond41_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bond41-31">[31]</a></sup> She acknowledges that she was overwhelmed when first arriving in first year, attributing this to the fact that neither of her parents had graduated from college,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> and that she had never spent time on a college campus.<sup id="cite_ref-TIME2015_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TIME2015-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>The mother of a white roommate reportedly unsuccessfully tried to get her daughter moved because of Michelle's race. She recalls her time at Princeton being the first time she was made more aware of her ethnicity and that despite the willingness of her classmates and teachers to want to understand her, she still felt "like a visitor on campus."<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> "I remember being shocked," she says, "by college students who drove <a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">BMWs</a>. I didn't even know parents who drove BMWs."<sup id="cite_ref-tn_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tn-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>While at Princeton, she got involved with the Third World Center (now known as the Carl A. Fields Center), an academic and cultural group that supported minority students, running their day care center, which also included after school tutoring.<sup id="cite_ref-Biography_Today_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Biography_Today-40">[40]</a></sup> She challenged the teaching methodology for French because she felt that it should be more conversational.<sup id="cite_ref-FWtWMO_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FWtWMO-41">[41]</a></sup> As part of her requirements for graduation, she wrote a thesis titled <i>Princeton-Educated Blacks and the Black Community.</i><sup id="cite_ref-thesis_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thesis-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> She researched her thesis by sending a questionnaire to African American graduates, requesting they specify when and how comfortable they were with their race prior to their enrollment at Princeton and how they felt about it when they were a student and since then. Of the 400 alumni to whom she sent the survey, fewer than 90 responded, and her findings did not support her hope that the black alumni would still identify with the African American community, even though they had attended an elite university with all of the advantages that accrues to its graduates.<sup id="cite_ref-Bond44_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bond44-44">[44]</a></sup> She majored in sociology and minored in <a href="/wiki/African_American_studies" class="mw-redirect" title="African American studies">African American studies</a>, graduating <i><a href="/wiki/Latin_honors" title="Latin honors">cum laude</a></i> with a Bachelor of Arts in 1985.<sup id="cite_ref-womanbehind_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-womanbehind-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>Robinson went on to earn her <a href="/wiki/Juris_Doctor" title="Juris Doctor">Juris Doctor</a> (J.D.) degree from <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Law_School" title="Harvard Law School">Harvard Law School</a> in 1988.<sup id="cite_ref-Princetonian_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Princetonian-46">[46]</a></sup> By the time she applied for Harvard Law, biographer Bond wrote, her confidence had grown; "This time around, there was no doubt in her mind that she had earned her place".<sup id="cite_ref-Bond44_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bond44-44">[44]</a></sup> Her faculty mentor at Harvard Law was <a href="/wiki/Charles_Ogletree" title="Charles Ogletree">Charles Ogletree</a>, who has said that she had answered the question that had plagued her throughout Princeton by the time she arrived at Harvard Law, of whether she would remain the product of her parents or keep the identity she had acquired at Princeton, believing that she concluded she could be "both brilliant and black."<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>At Harvard she participated in demonstrations advocating the hiring of professors who were members of minorities<sup id="cite_ref-Newsweek20080225_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newsweek20080225-48">[48]</a></sup> and worked for the <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Legal_Aid_Bureau" title="Harvard Legal Aid Bureau">Harvard Legal Aid Bureau</a>, assisting low-income tenants with housing cases.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> She is the third First Lady with a <a href="/wiki/Postgraduate_education" title="Postgraduate education">postgraduate degree</a>, after her two immediate predecessors, <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Laura_Bush" title="Laura Bush">Laura Bush</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-VLiCBTO_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VLiCBTO-50">[50]</a></sup> She would later say her education gave her opportunities beyond what she had ever imagined.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> In July 2008, she accepted the invitation to become an honorary member of the 100-year-old black sorority <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Kappa_Alpha" title="Alpha Kappa Alpha">Alpha Kappa Alpha</a>, which had no active undergraduate chapter at Princeton when she attended.<sup id="cite_ref-celebrate_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-celebrate-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Family_life">Family life</span></h3>
<p>Her father, Fraser C. Robinson III, died from complications from his illness in March 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> She would later say that although he was the "hole in my heart" and "loss in my scar", the memory of her father has motivated her each day since.<sup id="cite_ref-TIME2015_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TIME2015-37">[37]</a></sup> Her friend Suzanne Alele died from cancer around this time as well, Obama later telling <a href="/wiki/Katie_Couric" title="Katie Couric">Katie Couric</a> that the loss made her think of her contributions toward society and how well she was influencing the world from her law firm. This was seen as a turning point for Michelle.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>Michelle met Barack Obama when they were among the few African Americans at their law firm, <a href="/wiki/Sidley_Austin" title="Sidley Austin">Sidley Austin LLP</a> (she has sometimes said only two, although others have pointed out there were others in different departments),<sup id="cite_ref-WMMB_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WMMB-55">[55]</a></sup> and she was assigned to mentor him while he was a <a href="/wiki/Summer_associate" class="mw-redirect" title="Summer associate">summer associate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MOCT_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOCT-56">[56]</a></sup> Their relationship started with a business lunch and then a <a href="/wiki/Community_organization" title="Community organization">community organization</a> meeting where he first impressed her.<sup id="cite_ref-MOHSMOMF_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOHSMOMF-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before meeting Obama, Michelle had told her mother she would focus solely on her career.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> The couple's first date was to the <a href="/wiki/Spike_Lee" title="Spike Lee">Spike Lee</a> movie <i><a href="/wiki/Do_the_Right_Thing" title="Do the Right Thing">Do the Right Thing</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Barack Obama has opined that the two had an "opposites attract" scenario in their interest for each other initially since Michelle had stability through her two-parent home while he was "adventurous".<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> They married in October 1992,<sup id="cite_ref-MOHSMOMF_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOHSMOMF-57">[57]</a></sup> and have two daughters, Malia Ann (born 1998) and Natasha (known as Sasha, born 2001).<sup id="cite_ref-Newsweek2007_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newsweek2007-61">[61]</a></sup> Michelle Obama's mother, Marian Robinson was quoted by <i><a href="/wiki/Washington_Post" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington Post">Washington Post</a></i> correspondent <a href="/w/index.php?title=Peter_Slevin&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Peter Slevin (page does not exist)">Peter Slevin</a> in his book, <i>Michelle Obama: A Life</i><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> in an interview with <a href="/wiki/WTTW" title="WTTW">WTTW</a>'s <i>Chicago Tonight</i> in which Mrs Robinson addressed the issue of race. She told the interviewer that Barack Obama's mixed-race heritage did not worry her; "'That didn't concern me as much as had he been completely white."<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>After his election to the U.S. Senate, the Obama family continued to live on Chicago's South Side, choosing to remain there rather than moving to Washington, D.C. Throughout her husband's <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama_presidential_campaign,_2008" title="Barack Obama presidential campaign, 2008">2008 campaign for US President</a>, she made a "commitment to be away overnight only once a week&#160;– to campaign only two days a week and be home by the end of the second day" for their two daughters.<sup id="cite_ref-PasadenaWeekly_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PasadenaWeekly-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:236px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_family_portrait_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Barack_Obama_family_portrait_2011.jpg/234px-Barack_Obama_family_portrait_2011.jpg" width="234" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Barack_Obama_family_portrait_2011.jpg/351px-Barack_Obama_family_portrait_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Barack_Obama_family_portrait_2011.jpg/468px-Barack_Obama_family_portrait_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4096" data-file-height="2731" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_family_portrait_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Official portrait by <a href="/wiki/Pete_Souza" title="Pete Souza">Pete Souza</a> of the Obama family in the <a href="/wiki/Oval_Office" title="Oval Office">Oval Office</a>, December 11, 2011.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>She once requested that her then-fiancé meet her prospective boss, <a href="/wiki/Valerie_Jarrett" title="Valerie Jarrett">Valerie Jarrett</a>, when considering her first career move;<sup id="cite_ref-FLIW_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLIW-19">[19]</a></sup> Jarrett is now one of her husband's closest advisors.<sup id="cite_ref-MOIGaLM_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOIGaLM-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MOSHR_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOSHR-66">[66]</a></sup> The marital relationship has had its ebbs and flows; the combination of an evolving family life and beginning political career led to many arguments about balancing work and family. Barack Obama wrote in his second book, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Audacity_of_Hope:_Thoughts_on_Reclaiming_the_American_Dream" class="mw-redirect" title="The Audacity of Hope: Thoughts on Reclaiming the American Dream">The Audacity of Hope: Thoughts on Reclaiming the American Dream</a></i>, that "Tired and stressed, we had little time for conversation, much less romance."<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> However, despite their family obligations and careers, they continued to attempt to schedule date nights while they lived in Chicago.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Obamas' daughters attended the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago_Laboratory_Schools" title="University of Chicago Laboratory Schools">University of Chicago Laboratory Schools</a>, a private school.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> As a member of the school's board, Michelle fought to maintain diversity in the school when other board members connected with the University of Chicago tried to reserve more slots for children of the university faculty. This resulted in a plan to expand the school.<sup id="cite_ref-PAW2009_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PAW2009-5">[5]</a></sup> Malia and Sasha attended <a href="/wiki/Sidwell_Friends_School" title="Sidwell Friends School">Sidwell Friends School</a> in Washington, after also considering <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_Day_School" title="Georgetown Day School">Georgetown Day School</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Sidwell_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sidwell-70">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JOMF_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JOMF-71">[71]</a></sup> Michelle stated in an interview on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ellen_DeGeneres_Show" title="The Ellen DeGeneres Show">The Ellen DeGeneres Show</a></i> that they do not intend to have any more children.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> The Obamas have received advice from past first ladies <a href="/wiki/Laura_Bush" title="Laura Bush">Laura Bush</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rosalynn_Carter" title="Rosalynn Carter">Rosalynn Carter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> about raising children in the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-JOMF_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JOMF-71">[71]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Marian_Robinson" class="mw-redirect" title="Marian Robinson">Marian Robinson</a>, Michelle's mother, moved into the White House to assist with child care.<sup id="cite_ref-MOSWW_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOSWW-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:247px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Obamas_at_church_on_Inauguration_Day_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Obamas_at_church_on_Inauguration_Day_2013.jpg/245px-Obamas_at_church_on_Inauguration_Day_2013.jpg" width="245" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Obamas_at_church_on_Inauguration_Day_2013.jpg/368px-Obamas_at_church_on_Inauguration_Day_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Obamas_at_church_on_Inauguration_Day_2013.jpg/490px-Obamas_at_church_on_Inauguration_Day_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4040" data-file-height="2675" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Obamas_at_church_on_Inauguration_Day_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Obamas attend a church service in Washington, D.C., January 2013.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Michelle Obama was raised <a href="/wiki/United_Methodist" class="mw-redirect" title="United Methodist">United Methodist</a> and joined the <a href="/wiki/Trinity_United_Church_of_Christ" title="Trinity United Church of Christ">Trinity United Church of Christ</a>, where she and Barack Obama married, performed by <a href="/wiki/Jeremiah_Wright" title="Jeremiah Wright">Jeremiah Wright</a>. On May 31, 2008, Barack and Michelle Obama announced that they had withdrawn their membership in Trinity United Church of Christ stating: "Our relations with Trinity have been strained by the divisive statements of Reverend Wright, which sharply conflict with our own views."<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Obama family has attended several different Protestant churches since moving to Washington D.C. in 2009, including <a href="/wiki/Shiloh_Baptist_Church_(Washington,_D.C.)" title="Shiloh Baptist Church (Washington, D.C.)">Shiloh Baptist Church</a> and <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s_Episcopal_Church,_Lafayette_Square_(Washington,_D.C.)" class="mw-redirect" title="St. John's Episcopal Church, Lafayette Square (Washington, D.C.)">St. John's Episcopal Church</a>. At the 49th <a href="/wiki/African_Methodist_Episcopal_Church" title="African Methodist Episcopal Church">African Methodist Episcopal Church</a>'s general conference, Michelle Obama encouraged the attendees to advocate for political awareness, saying, "To anyone who says that church is no place to talk about these issues, you tell them there is no place better&#160;– no place better, because ultimately, these are not just political issues&#160;– they are moral issues, they're issues that have to do with human dignity and human potential, and the future we want for our kids and our grandkids."<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span></h2>
<p>Following law school, she was an associate at the Chicago office of the law firm <a href="/wiki/Sidley_Austin" title="Sidley Austin">Sidley &amp; Austin</a>, where she first met her future husband. At the firm, she worked on marketing and intellectual property.<sup id="cite_ref-womanbehind_4-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-womanbehind-4">[4]</a></sup> She continues to hold her <a href="/wiki/Law_license" class="mw-redirect" title="Law license">law license</a>, but as she no longer needs it for her work, it has been on a voluntary inactive status since 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1991, she held <a href="/wiki/Public_sector" title="Public sector">public sector</a> positions in the Chicago city government as an Assistant to the <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Chicago" title="Mayor of Chicago">Mayor</a>, and as Assistant Commissioner of Planning and Development. In 1993, she became Executive Director for the Chicago office of <a href="/wiki/Public_Allies" title="Public Allies">Public Allies</a>, a non-profit organization encouraging young people to work on social issues in nonprofit groups and government agencies.<sup id="cite_ref-West_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-West-26">[26]</a></sup> She worked there nearly four years and set <a href="/wiki/Fundraising" title="Fundraising">fundraising</a> records for the organization that still stood 12 years after she left.<sup id="cite_ref-MOSS_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOSS-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1996, Obama served as the Associate Dean of Student Services at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">University of Chicago</a>, where she developed the University's Community Service Center.<sup id="cite_ref-UCChron96_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UCChron96-78">[78]</a></sup> In 2002, she began working for the University of Chicago Hospitals, first as executive director for community affairs and, beginning May 2005, as Vice President for Community and External Affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-UChicago2005_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UChicago2005-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>She continued to hold the University of Chicago Hospitals position during the primary campaign, but cut back to part-time in order to spend time with her daughters as well as work for her husband's election;<sup id="cite_ref-ABCNews20080124_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABCNews20080124-80">[80]</a></sup> she subsequently took a leave of absence from her job.<sup id="cite_ref-blaze_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blaze-81">[81]</a></sup> According to the couple's 2006 <a href="/wiki/Tax_return_(United_States)" title="Tax return (United States)">income tax return</a>, her salary was $273,618 from the University of Chicago Hospitals, while her husband had a salary of $157,082 from the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">United States Senate</a>. The Obamas' total income, however, was $991,296, which included $51,200 she earned as a member of the board of directors of <a href="/wiki/TreeHouse_Foods" title="TreeHouse Foods">TreeHouse Foods</a>, and investments and royalties from his books.<sup id="cite_ref-MOChw_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOChw-82">[82]</a></sup> Obama stated that she had never been happier in her life prior to working "to build Public Allies".<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>Obama served as a salaried board member of <a href="/wiki/TreeHouse_Foods" title="TreeHouse Foods">TreeHouse Foods</a>, Inc. (<a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">NYSE</a>:&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nyse.com/quote/XNYS:THS">THS</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-TreeHouse_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TreeHouse-84">[84]</a></sup> a major <a href="/wiki/Wal-Mart" class="mw-redirect" title="Wal-Mart">Wal-Mart</a> supplier with which she cut ties immediately after her husband made comments critical of Wal-Mart at an <a href="/wiki/AFL-CIO" class="mw-redirect" title="AFL-CIO">AFL-CIO</a> forum in <a href="/wiki/Trenton,_New_Jersey" title="Trenton, New Jersey">Trenton, New Jersey</a>, on May 14, 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-SunTimesBlog200705_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SunTimesBlog200705-85">[85]</a></sup> She also served on the board of directors of the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Council_on_Global_Affairs" title="Chicago Council on Global Affairs">Chicago Council on Global Affairs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ChicagoCouncil_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChicagoCouncil-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Barack_Obama_political_campaigns">Barack Obama political campaigns</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_campaigns">Early campaigns</span></h3>
<p>During an interview in 1996, Michelle Obama acknowledged there was a "strong possibility" her husband would begin a political career, but said she was "wary" of the process due to it meaning that their lives would become "an open book" while she was private.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although she has campaigned on her husband's behalf since early in his political career by handshaking and fund-raising, she did not relish the activity at first. When she campaigned during <a href="/wiki/Illinois_Senate_career_of_Barack_Obama#Campaign_for_Bobby_Rush.27s_congressional_seat" title="Illinois Senate career of Barack Obama">her husband's 2000 run</a> for <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">United States House of Representatives</a>, her boss at the University of Chicago asked if there was any single thing about campaigning that she enjoyed; after some thought, she replied that visiting so many living rooms had given her some new <a href="/wiki/Interior_decoration" class="mw-redirect" title="Interior decoration">decorating</a> ideas.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT0825_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT0825-88">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> Obama opposed her husband's run for the congressional seat, and, after his defeat, she preferred he tend to the financial needs of the family in what she deemed a more practical way.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2008_Presidential_campaign">2008 Presidential campaign</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:377px;max-width:377px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Michelle_Obama_and_Barack_Obama_enjoy_a_victory_fist_pound_upon_winning_the_Democratic_Nomination.jpg" class="image"><img alt="The Obamas face each other and bump fists on stage. She wears a purple dress and he wears a dark suit. Several signs read &quot;CHANGE WE CAN BELIEVE IN&quot; and several photographers take photos." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Michelle_Obama_and_Barack_Obama_enjoy_a_victory_fist_pound_upon_winning_the_Democratic_Nomination.jpg/180px-Michelle_Obama_and_Barack_Obama_enjoy_a_victory_fist_pound_upon_winning_the_Democratic_Nomination.jpg" width="180" height="155" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e8/Michelle_Obama_and_Barack_Obama_enjoy_a_victory_fist_pound_upon_winning_the_Democratic_Nomination.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="250" data-file-height="215" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The Obamas <a href="/wiki/Fist_bump" title="Fist bump">fist bump</a> upon his winning the Democratic nomination.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:191px;max-width:191px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Obamas_and_Bidens.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Barack and Michelle Obama and a woman and a man on an outdoor stage. The first three smile and wave. The men wear suit pants, white shirts with the sleeves rolled up, and ties. Michelle is in a colorful print dress and the other woman is in a creme business suit." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Obamas_and_Bidens.jpg/189px-Obamas_and_Bidens.jpg" width="189" height="154" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Obamas_and_Bidens.jpg/284px-Obamas_and_Bidens.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Obamas_and_Bidens.jpg/378px-Obamas_and_Bidens.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3559" data-file-height="2901" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The Obamas, with <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Joe</a> and Dr. <a href="/wiki/Jill_Biden" title="Jill Biden">Jill Biden</a>, at the August 23, 2008 Vice Presidential announcement in <a href="/wiki/Springfield,_Illinois" title="Springfield, Illinois">Springfield, Illinois</a>.</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At first, Obama had reservations about her husband's presidential campaign, due to fears about a possible negative effect on their daughters.<sup id="cite_ref-MONYT_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MONYT-91">[91]</a></sup> She says that she negotiated an agreement in which her husband was to quit smoking in exchange for her support of his decision to run.<sup id="cite_ref-MOoCF_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOoCF-92">[92]</a></sup> About her role in her husband's presidential campaign she has said: "My job is not a senior adviser".<sup id="cite_ref-MOIGaLM_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOIGaLM-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MOpuric_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOpuric-93">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> During the campaign, she has discussed race and education by using motherhood as a framework.<sup id="cite_ref-FWtWMO_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FWtWMO-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2007, three months after her husband declared his presidential candidacy, Obama reduced her professional responsibilities by 80 percent to support his presidential campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-FLIW_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLIW-19">[19]</a></sup> Early in the campaign, she had limited involvement in which she traveled to political events only two days a week and rarely traveled overnight;<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> by early February 2008 her participation had increased significantly, attending thirty-three events in eight days.<sup id="cite_ref-MOSHR_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOSHR-66">[66]</a></sup> She made several campaign appearances with <a href="/wiki/Oprah_Winfrey" title="Oprah Winfrey">Oprah Winfrey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> She wrote her own <a href="/wiki/Stump_speech_(politics)" title="Stump speech (politics)">stump speeches</a> for her husband's presidential campaign and generally spoke without notes.<sup id="cite_ref-tn_27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tn-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the campaign, columnist <a href="/wiki/Cal_Thomas" title="Cal Thomas">Cal Thomas</a> on <a href="/wiki/Fox_News" title="Fox News">Fox News</a> labeled Michelle Obama as an "<a href="/wiki/Angry_Black_Woman" title="Angry Black Woman">Angry Black Woman</a>"<sup id="cite_ref-AAMOLfaNI_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AAMOLfaNI-98">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> and some web sites attempted to propagate this image,<sup id="cite_ref-MUM_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MUM-101">[101]</a></sup> prompting her to respond: "Barack and I have been in the public eye for many years now, and we've developed a thick skin along the way. When you're out campaigning, there will always be criticism. I just take it in stride, and at the end of the day, I know that it comes with the territory."<sup id="cite_ref-WatsonCovarrubias2012_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WatsonCovarrubias2012-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>By the time of the <a href="/wiki/2008_Democratic_National_Convention" title="2008 Democratic National Convention">2008 Democratic National Convention</a> in August, media outlets observed that her presence on the campaign trail had grown softer than at the start of the race, focusing on soliciting concerns and empathizing with the audience rather than throwing down challenges to them, and giving interviews to shows like <i><a href="/wiki/The_View_(U.S._TV_series)" title="The View (U.S. TV series)">The View</a></i> and publications like <i><a href="/wiki/Ladies%27_Home_Journal" title="Ladies' Home Journal">Ladies' Home Journal</a></i> rather than appearing on news programs. The change was even reflected in her fashion choices, wearing more informal clothes in place of her previous designer pieces.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT0825_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT0825-88">[88]</a></sup> The <i>View</i> appearance was partly intended to help soften her public image,<sup id="cite_ref-AAMOLfaNI_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AAMOLfaNI-98">[98]</a></sup> and it was widely covered in the press.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>The presidential campaign was Obama's first exposure to the national political scene; even before the field of <a href="/wiki/United_States_Democratic_presidential_candidates,_2008" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Democratic presidential candidates, 2008">Democratic candidates</a> was narrowed to two, she was considered the least famous of the candidates' spouses.<sup id="cite_ref-MOpuric_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOpuric-93">[93]</a></sup> Early in the campaign, she told anecdotes about the Obama family life; however, as the press began to emphasize her sarcasm, she toned it down.<sup id="cite_ref-MOChw_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOChw-82">[82]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MOoCF_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOoCF-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>New York Times</i> <a href="/wiki/Editorial" title="Editorial">op-ed</a> columnist <a href="/wiki/Maureen_Dowd" title="Maureen Dowd">Maureen Dowd</a> wrote:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>I wince a bit when Michelle Obama chides her husband as a mere mortal&#160;– a comic routine that rests on the presumption that we see him as a god&#160;... But it may not be smart politics to mock him in a way that turns him from the glam <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">JFK</a> into the mundane <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Ford" title="Gerald Ford">Gerald Ford</a>, toasting his own English muffin. If all Senator Obama is peddling is the <a href="/wiki/Camelot_era" class="mw-redirect" title="Camelot era">Camelot</a> mystique, why debunk this mystique?<sup id="cite_ref-MOpuric_93-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOpuric-93">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:375px;max-width:375px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Michelle,_Oprah_Winfrey_and_Barack_Obama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Michelle Obama, Oprah Winfrey and Barack Obama on stage at a campaign rally." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Michelle%2C_Oprah_Winfrey_and_Barack_Obama.jpg/180px-Michelle%2C_Oprah_Winfrey_and_Barack_Obama.jpg" width="180" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Michelle%2C_Oprah_Winfrey_and_Barack_Obama.jpg/270px-Michelle%2C_Oprah_Winfrey_and_Barack_Obama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Michelle%2C_Oprah_Winfrey_and_Barack_Obama.jpg/360px-Michelle%2C_Oprah_Winfrey_and_Barack_Obama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4368" data-file-height="2912" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Oprah_Winfrey%27s_endorsement_of_Barack_Obama" title="Oprah Winfrey's endorsement of Barack Obama">Oprah Winfrey joins the Obamas</a> on the campaign trail, December 10, 2007.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:189px;max-width:189px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Michelle_Obama_DNC_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Michelle Obama speaks at a convention; her image and name are projected on a huge screen behind her. The large audience waves vertical blue signs." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Michelle_Obama_DNC_2008.jpg/187px-Michelle_Obama_DNC_2008.jpg" width="187" height="119" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Michelle_Obama_DNC_2008.jpg/281px-Michelle_Obama_DNC_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Michelle_Obama_DNC_2008.jpg/374px-Michelle_Obama_DNC_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3644" data-file-height="2313" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Obama speaks at the 2008 Democratic convention.</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On the first night of the <a href="/wiki/2008_Democratic_National_Convention" title="2008 Democratic National Convention">2008 Democratic National Convention</a>, <a href="/wiki/Craig_Robinson_(basketball)" title="Craig Robinson (basketball)">Craig Robinson</a> introduced his younger sister.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> She delivered her speech, during which she sought to portray herself and her family as the embodiment of the <a href="/wiki/American_Dream" title="American Dream">American Dream</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT0826_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT0826-106">[106]</a></sup> Obama said she and her husband believe "that you work hard for what you want in life, that your word is your bond, and you do what you say you're going to do, that you treat people with dignity and respect, even if you don't know them, and even if you don't agree with them."<sup id="cite_ref-NPR0826_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NPR0826-107">[107]</a></sup> She also emphasized loving her country, in response to criticism for her previous statements about feeling proud of her country for the first time,<sup id="cite_ref-NYT0826_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT0826-106">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CST0826_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CST0826-108">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BG0826_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BG0826-109">[109]</a></sup> where the original statement was seen as a gaffe.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> That keynote address was largely well-received and drew mostly positive reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Rasmussen_Reports" title="Rasmussen Reports">Rasmussen Reports</a> poll found that her favorability among Americans reached 55%.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>On an October 6, 2008 broadcast, <a href="/wiki/Larry_King" title="Larry King">Larry King</a> asked Obama if the American electorate was past the <a href="/wiki/Bradley_effect" title="Bradley effect">Bradley effect</a>. She stated that her husband's achievement of the nomination was a fairly strong indicator that it was.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> The same night she was interviewed by <a href="/wiki/Jon_Stewart" title="Jon Stewart">Jon Stewart</a> on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Show" title="The Daily Show">The Daily Show</a></i> where she deflected criticism of her husband and his campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> On Fox News' <i><a href="/wiki/America%27s_Pulse" class="mw-redirect" title="America's Pulse">America's Pulse</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/E._D._Hill" title="E. D. Hill">E. D. Hill</a> referred to the <a href="/wiki/Fist_bump" title="Fist bump">fist bump</a> shared by the Obamas on the night that he clinched the <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama_presidential_primary_campaign,_2008" title="Barack Obama presidential primary campaign, 2008">Democratic presidential nomination</a> as a "terrorist fist jab"; Hill was taken off air and the show itself was cancelled.<sup id="cite_ref-FrtMOabm_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FrtMOabm-115">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2012_Presidential_re-election_campaign">2012 Presidential re-election campaign</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Obamas_and_Bidens_on_presidential_election_night_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Obamas_and_Bidens_on_presidential_election_night_2012.jpg/220px-Obamas_and_Bidens_on_presidential_election_night_2012.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Obamas_and_Bidens_on_presidential_election_night_2012.jpg/330px-Obamas_and_Bidens_on_presidential_election_night_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Obamas_and_Bidens_on_presidential_election_night_2012.jpg/440px-Obamas_and_Bidens_on_presidential_election_night_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4096" data-file-height="2731" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Obamas_and_Bidens_on_presidential_election_night_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Obama (far right) celebrates with <a href="/wiki/Jill_Biden" title="Jill Biden">Jill Biden</a> after their husbands win re-election.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Obama campaigned for her husband's re-election in 2012. Beginning in 2011, Obama became more politically active than she had been since the 2008 election, though avoided discussions about the re-election bid.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> By the time of the election cycle, she had developed a more open public image,<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> some viewing her as the most popular member of the Obama administration,<sup id="cite_ref-2012POLITICO_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012POLITICO-121">[121]</a></sup> as her poll numbers having never dropped below 60% since entering the White House<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> and an Obama senior campaign official even dubbed her "the most popular political figure in America".<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> The positive assessment was reasoned to have contributed to her active role in the re-election campaign, but it was noted that the challenge for the Obama campaign was using her without tarnishing her popularity. Obama was viewed as a polarizing figure, having both "sharp enmity and deep loyalty" from Americans, but she was also seen as having improved her image since the time of the last election when her husband initially ran for the presidency.<sup id="cite_ref-2012POLITICO_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012POLITICO-121">[121]</a></sup> It was commented by Isabel Wilkinson of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Beast" title="The Daily Beast">The Daily Beast</a></i> that her style changed over the course of the campaign to sensitive and economical.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<p>Obama expressed confidence in her husband's debating skills prior to the first debate of the election cycle,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> though his performance would later be criticized as appearing detached and for looking down when addressing Romney,<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> leading to a consensus that the latter won the debate.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> After her speech at the <a href="/wiki/2012_Democratic_National_Convention" title="2012 Democratic National Convention">2012 Democratic National Convention</a>, Obama was found through a CBS News/New York Times poll conducted in September to have a 61% favorably rating with registered voters, the highest favorability she had sustained since April 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> Obama aimed to humanize her husband with relating stories about him, attempting to appeal to female voters in swing states. It was commented by Paul Harris of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> that the same tactic was being used by <a href="/wiki/Ann_Romney" title="Ann Romney">Ann Romney</a>, wife of 2012 Republican presidential candidate <a href="/wiki/Mitt_Romney" title="Mitt Romney">Mitt Romney</a>. Polls in October showed their husbands tied at 47% for the female vote. However, Michelle Obama's favorability ratings remained higher than Ann Romney's at 69% to 52%.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> Despite Obama's higher poll numbers, comparisons between Obama and Romney were consistently made by the media until the election,<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> regardless of Michelle Cottle of <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i> writing, "nobody votes for first lady."<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="First_Lady_of_the_United_States">First Lady of the United States</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:458px;max-width:458px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:227px;max-width:227px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Barack_Obama_Michelle_Obama_Queen_Elizabeth_II_Buckingham_Palace_London.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Michelle Obama and Elizabeth II shake hands and smile at each other as Barack enters the room in the background." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Barack_Obama_Michelle_Obama_Queen_Elizabeth_II_Buckingham_Palace_London.jpg/225px-Barack_Obama_Michelle_Obama_Queen_Elizabeth_II_Buckingham_Palace_London.jpg" width="225" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Barack_Obama_Michelle_Obama_Queen_Elizabeth_II_Buckingham_Palace_London.jpg/338px-Barack_Obama_Michelle_Obama_Queen_Elizabeth_II_Buckingham_Palace_London.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Barack_Obama_Michelle_Obama_Queen_Elizabeth_II_Buckingham_Palace_London.jpg/450px-Barack_Obama_Michelle_Obama_Queen_Elizabeth_II_Buckingham_Palace_London.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3500" data-file-height="2333" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Obama is greeted by <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Elizabeth II of the United Kingdom">Queen Elizabeth II</a> at <a href="/wiki/Buckingham_Palace" title="Buckingham Palace">Buckingham Palace</a>, United Kingdom April 1, 2009.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:227px;max-width:227px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Michelle_obama_and_carla_bruni_sarkozy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Michelle Obama and Carla Bruni share a laugh while seated on adjacent couches." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Michelle_obama_and_carla_bruni_sarkozy.jpg/225px-Michelle_obama_and_carla_bruni_sarkozy.jpg" width="225" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Michelle_obama_and_carla_bruni_sarkozy.jpg/338px-Michelle_obama_and_carla_bruni_sarkozy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Michelle_obama_and_carla_bruni_sarkozy.jpg/450px-Michelle_obama_and_carla_bruni_sarkozy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3500" data-file-height="2333" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Michelle Obama and <a href="/wiki/Carla_Bruni" title="Carla Bruni">Carla Bruni</a> at <a href="/wiki/Palais_Rohan,_Strasbourg" title="Palais Rohan, Strasbourg">Palais Rohan, Strasbourg</a>, France April 3, 2009.</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During her early months as First Lady, Obama visited <a href="/wiki/Homeless_shelter" title="Homeless shelter">homeless shelters</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soup_kitchen" title="Soup kitchen">soup kitchens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MIFOTS_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MIFOTS-134">[134]</a></sup> She also sent representatives to schools and advocated public service.<sup id="cite_ref-MIFOTS_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MIFOTS-134">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<p>Obama advocated for her husband's policy priorities by promoting bills that support it. She hosted a White House reception for women's rights advocates in celebration of the enactment of the <a href="/wiki/Lilly_Ledbetter_Fair_Pay_Act_of_2009" title="Lilly Ledbetter Fair Pay Act of 2009">Lilly Ledbetter Fair Pay Act of 2009</a> <a href="/wiki/Pay_equity" class="mw-redirect" title="Pay equity">Pay equity</a> law. She supported the economic stimulus bill in visits to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Housing_and_Urban_Development" title="United States Department of Housing and Urban Development">United States Department of Housing and Urban Development</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Education" title="United States Department of Education">United States Department of Education</a>. Some observers looked favorably upon her legislative activities, while others said that she should be less involved in politics. According to her representatives, she intended to visit all <a href="/wiki/United_States_Cabinet" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Cabinet">United States Cabinet</a>-level agencies in order to get acquainted with Washington.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Army_53373_First_Lady_Embarks_on_Mission_to_Help_Military_Families.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/US_Army_53373_First_Lady_Embarks_on_Mission_to_Help_Military_Families.jpg/220px-US_Army_53373_First_Lady_Embarks_on_Mission_to_Help_Military_Families.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/US_Army_53373_First_Lady_Embarks_on_Mission_to_Help_Military_Families.jpg/330px-US_Army_53373_First_Lady_Embarks_on_Mission_to_Help_Military_Families.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/US_Army_53373_First_Lady_Embarks_on_Mission_to_Help_Military_Families.jpg/440px-US_Army_53373_First_Lady_Embarks_on_Mission_to_Help_Military_Families.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="399" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Army_53373_First_Lady_Embarks_on_Mission_to_Help_Military_Families.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Obama and General Charles R. Davis smile to the crowd before speaking on her mission to help military families, October 2009.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On June 5, 2009, the White House announced that Michelle Obama was replacing her then chief of staff, <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Norris" title="Jackie Norris">Jackie Norris</a>, with <a href="/w/index.php?title=Susan_Sher&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Susan Sher (page does not exist)">Susan Sher</a>, a longtime friend and adviser. Norris became a senior adviser to the <a href="/wiki/Corporation_for_National_and_Community_Service" title="Corporation for National and Community Service">Corporation for National and Community Service</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> Another key aide, <a href="/wiki/Spelman_College" title="Spelman College">Spelman College</a> alumna Kristen Jarvis, served from 2008 until 2015, when she left to become chief of staff to the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Foundation" title="Ford Foundation">Ford Foundation</a> president <a href="/wiki/Darren_Walker" title="Darren Walker">Darren Walker</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2009 Michelle Obama was named <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Walters" title="Barbara Walters">Barbara Walters</a>' <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Walters%27_10_Most_Fascinating_People" title="Barbara Walters' 10 Most Fascinating People">Most Fascinating Person</a> of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some initiatives of First Lady Michelle Obama include advocating on behalf of military families, helping working women balance career and family, encouraging national service, and promoting the arts and arts education.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MOMMFHM_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOMMFHM-141">[141]</a></sup> Obama made supporting military families and spouses a personal mission and has been increasingly bonding with military families. According to her aides, stories of the sacrifice these families make moved her to tears.<sup id="cite_ref-MOMMFHM_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOMMFHM-141">[141]</a></sup> In April 2012, Obama and her husband were awarded the Jerald Washington Memorial Founders' Award by the <a href="/wiki/National_Coalition_for_Homeless_Veterans" title="National Coalition for Homeless Veterans">National Coalition for Homeless Veterans</a> (NCHV).The award is the highest honor given to homeless veteran advocates.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> Obama was again honored with the award in May 2015, accepting with <a href="/wiki/Jill_Biden" title="Jill Biden">Jill Biden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Michelle-obama-bringbackourgirls.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Michelle-obama-bringbackourgirls.jpg/220px-Michelle-obama-bringbackourgirls.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Michelle-obama-bringbackourgirls.jpg/330px-Michelle-obama-bringbackourgirls.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Michelle-obama-bringbackourgirls.jpg/440px-Michelle-obama-bringbackourgirls.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1023" data-file-height="682" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Michelle-obama-bringbackourgirls.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Obama holding a sign with the hashtag "#bringbackourgirls" in May 2014.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Melania_Trump_with_Michelle_Obama_at_the_White_House_(crop).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Melania_Trump_with_Michelle_Obama_at_the_White_House_%28crop%29.jpg/220px-Melania_Trump_with_Michelle_Obama_at_the_White_House_%28crop%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Melania_Trump_with_Michelle_Obama_at_the_White_House_%28crop%29.jpg/330px-Melania_Trump_with_Michelle_Obama_at_the_White_House_%28crop%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Melania_Trump_with_Michelle_Obama_at_the_White_House_%28crop%29.jpg/440px-Melania_Trump_with_Michelle_Obama_at_the_White_House_%28crop%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2015" data-file-height="1515" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Melania_Trump_with_Michelle_Obama_at_the_White_House_(crop).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Obama meets future First Lady <a href="/wiki/Melania_Trump" title="Melania Trump">Melania Trump</a> in November 2016.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In November 2013, a <i><a href="/wiki/Politico" title="Politico">Politico</a></i> article by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Michelle_Cottle&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Michelle Cottle (page does not exist)">Michelle Cottle</a> accusing Obama of being a "feminist nightmare" for not using her position and education to advocate for women's issues was sharply criticized across the political spectrum.<sup id="cite_ref-miccot2013_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-miccot2013-144">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Harris-Perry_2013_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harris-Perry_2013-145">[145]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-howkur2013_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-howkur2013-146">[146]</a></sup> Cottle quoted <a href="/wiki/Linda_Hirshman" title="Linda Hirshman">Linda Hirshman</a> saying of Obama's trendy styles, promotion of gardening and healthy eating, and support of military families that "She essentially became the English lady of the manor, Tory Party, circa 1830s."<sup id="cite_ref-miccot2013_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-miccot2013-144">[144]</a></sup> A prominent critic of Cottle was <a href="/wiki/MSNBC" title="MSNBC">MSNBC</a> host Melissa Harris-Perry, who rhetorically asked "Are you serious?"<sup id="cite_ref-Harris-Perry_2013_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harris-Perry_2013-145">[145]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-howkur2013_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-howkur2013-146">[146]</a></sup> Supporters of Obama note that the First Lady had been one of the only people in the administration to address <a href="/wiki/Obesity" title="Obesity">obesity</a>, through promoting good eating habits, which is one of the leading US public health crises.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2014, Obama joined the campaign to bring back school girls who had been <a href="/wiki/Chibok_schoolgirls_kidnapping" title="Chibok schoolgirls kidnapping">kidnapped in Nigeria</a>. The First Lady tweeted a picture of herself holding a poster with the #bringbackourgirls campaign hashtag.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<p>Over the course of the Obama presidency, particularly during the second term, Michelle Obama was subject to speculation over whether she would run for the presidency herself, similarly to predecessor Hillary Clinton.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> A potential Michelle Obama candidacy was supported by both <a href="/wiki/Samuel_L._Jackson" title="Samuel L. Jackson">Samuel L. Jackson</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Clyburn" class="mw-redirect" title="James Clyburn">James Clyburn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> On April 6, 2009, CNN did a poll on whether she should run for the presidency in 2020, 83% of responders being opposed to the idea.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> A May 2015 Rasmussen poll found Obama had 22% of support to Clinton's 56% of winning the Democratic nomination, higher than that of potential candidates <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Warren" title="Elizabeth Warren">Elizabeth Warren</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martin_O%27Malley" title="Martin O'Malley">Martin O'Malley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Sanders" title="Bernie Sanders">Bernie Sanders</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> Another poll from that month found 71% of Americans believed that Obama should not run for the presidency, only 14% approving.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> On January 14, 2016, during a town-hall meeting, President Obama was asked if the First Lady could be talked into running. He responded, "There are three things that are certain in life: death, taxes, and Michelle is not running for president. That I can tell you."<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> On March 16, 2016, while speaking in <a href="/wiki/Austin,_Texas" title="Austin, Texas">Austin, Texas</a>, Obama denied that she would ever run for the office, citing a desire to "impact as many people as possible in an unbiased way."<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Let's_Move!"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Let.27s_Move.21"><i>Let's Move!</i></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Let%27s_Move!" title="Let's Move!">Let's Move!</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:238px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Obama-DeGeneres-dance-20120201.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Obama-DeGeneres-dance-20120201.jpg/236px-Obama-DeGeneres-dance-20120201.jpg" width="236" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Obama-DeGeneres-dance-20120201.jpg/354px-Obama-DeGeneres-dance-20120201.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Obama-DeGeneres-dance-20120201.jpg/472px-Obama-DeGeneres-dance-20120201.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4096" data-file-height="2731" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Obama-DeGeneres-dance-20120201.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Obama and <a href="/wiki/Ellen_DeGeneres" title="Ellen DeGeneres">Ellen DeGeneres</a> dance on the second anniversary of <i><a href="/wiki/Let%27s_Move!" title="Let's Move!">Let's Move!</a></i>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Obama's predecessors Hillary Clinton and Laura Bush supported the <a href="/wiki/Organic_movement" title="Organic movement">organic movement</a> by instructing the White House kitchens to buy <a href="/wiki/Organic_food" title="Organic food">organic food</a>, and Obama extended their efforts toward healthy eating by planting the <a href="/wiki/White_House_Kitchen_Garden" class="mw-redirect" title="White House Kitchen Garden">White House Kitchen Garden</a>, an organic garden, the first White House vegetable garden since <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_Roosevelt" title="Eleanor Roosevelt">Eleanor Roosevelt</a> served as First Lady, and installing bee hives, on the South Lawn of the White House. The garden supplied organic produce and honey to the First Family and for state dinners and other official gatherings.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-garden_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-garden-159">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AaYoLtFLSOaL_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AaYoLtFLSOaL-160">[160]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2010, Obama undertook her first lead role in an administration-wide initiative, which she named "<i><a href="/wiki/Let%27s_Move!" title="Let's Move!">Let's Move!</a></i>," to make progress in reversing the 21st century trend of <a href="/wiki/Childhood_obesity" title="Childhood obesity">childhood obesity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AaYoLtFLSOaL_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AaYoLtFLSOaL-160">[160]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> On February 9, 2010, the First Lady announced <i>Let's Move!</i> and President Barack Obama created the <a href="/wiki/Task_Force_on_Childhood_Obesity" title="Task Force on Childhood Obesity">Task Force on Childhood Obesity</a> to review all current programs and create a national plan towards change.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> Michelle Obama stated that her goal was to make this effort her legacy: "I want to leave something behind that we can say, 'Because of this time that this person spent here, this thing has changed.' And my hope is that that's going to be in the area of childhood obesity."<sup id="cite_ref-AaYoLtFLSOaL_160-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AaYoLtFLSOaL-160">[160]</a></sup> Her 2012 book <i><a href="/wiki/American_Grown:_The_Story_of_the_White_House_Kitchen_Garden_and_Gardens_Across_America" class="mw-redirect" title="American Grown: The Story of the White House Kitchen Garden and Gardens Across America">American Grown: The Story of the White House Kitchen Garden and Gardens Across America</a></i> is based on her experiences with the garden and promotes healthy eating.<sup id="cite_ref-Benac_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Benac-164">[164]</a></sup> Her call for action on healthy eating has been echoed by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">United States Department of Defense</a>, which has been facing an ever-expanding problem of recruit obesity.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>Several Republicans have critiqued or lampooned Obama's initiative.
