In October 2014, senator <a href="/wiki/Rand_Paul" title="Rand Paul">Rand Paul</a> linked to Michelle Obama's Twitter account when announcing on the website that he was going to <a href="/wiki/Dunkin%27_Donuts" title="Dunkin' Donuts">Dunkin' Donuts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> In January 2016, Republican <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_New_Jersey" title="Governor of New Jersey">Governor of New Jersey</a> and presidential candidate <a href="/wiki/Chris_Christie" title="Chris Christie">Chris Christie</a> condemned the First Lady's involvement with healthy eating while on the campaign trail in <a href="/wiki/Iowa" title="Iowa">Iowa</a>, arguing that she was using the government to exercise her views on eating.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> Obama had previously cited Christie as an example of an adult who struggled with obesity, a demographic she sought to diminish by targeting children since <i>Let's Move!</i> was "working with kids when they're young, so that they don't have these direct challenges when they get older."<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> In February, Senator <a href="/wiki/Ted_Cruz" title="Ted Cruz">Ted Cruz</a> indicated that Obama's health policies would end under his administration, promising that french fries would return to cafeterias if his wife was First Lady.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="LGBT_rights">LGBT rights</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:229px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Michelle_Obama_official_portrait.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Michelle_Obama_official_portrait.jpg/227px-Michelle_Obama_official_portrait.jpg" width="227" height="340" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Michelle_Obama_official_portrait.jpg/340px-Michelle_Obama_official_portrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Michelle_Obama_official_portrait.jpg/453px-Michelle_Obama_official_portrait.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2222" data-file-height="3332" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Michelle_Obama_official_portrait.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Obama's first term official portrait.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the 2008 US presidential election, Obama boasted, to gay Democrat groups, of her husband's record on LGBT rights: his support of the Illinois Human Rights Act, the Illinois gender violence act, the <a href="/wiki/Employment_Non-Discrimination_Act" title="Employment Non-Discrimination Act">Employment Non-Discrimination Act</a>, repealing <a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Ask_Don%27t_Tell" class="mw-redirect" title="Don't Ask Don't Tell">Don't Ask Don't Tell</a>, and full repeal of the <a href="/wiki/Defense_of_Marriage_Act" title="Defense of Marriage Act">Defense of Marriage Act</a>, <a href="/wiki/Civil_unions" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil unions">civil unions</a>; along with hate crimes protection for sexual orientation and gender identity and renewed effort to fight <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV and AIDS</a>. They have both been opponents of constitutional amendments banning same-sex marriage in the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Marriage_Amendment" title="Federal Marriage Amendment">federal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Proposition_8" class="mw-redirect" title="Proposition 8">California</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Florida_Amendment_2" class="mw-redirect" title="Florida Amendment 2">Florida</a> constitutions. She said that the US Supreme Court delivered justice in the <i><a href="/wiki/Lawrence_v._Texas" title="Lawrence v. Texas">Lawrence v. Texas</a></i> case and drew a connection between the struggles for gay rights and civil rights by stating "We are all only here because of those who marched and bled and died, from Selma to Stonewall, in the pursuit of a more perfect union."<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the repeal of <a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Ask_Don%27t_Tell" class="mw-redirect" title="Don't Ask Don't Tell">Don't Ask Don't Tell</a> on September 20, 2011, Obama included openly gay service members in her national military families initiative.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> On May 9, 2012, Barack and Michelle Obama came out publicly in favor of same-sex marriage. Prior to this, Michelle Obama had never stated her position on same-sex marriage publicly. Senior White House officials said that Michelle Obama and Senior Adviser <a href="/wiki/Valerie_Jarrett" title="Valerie Jarrett">Valerie Jarrett</a> had been the two most consistent advocates for same-sex marriage in Barack Obama's life.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> Michelle went on to say that "This is an important issue for millions of <a href="/wiki/Americans" title="Americans">Americans</a>, and for Barack and me, it really comes down to the values of fairness and equality we want to pass down to our girls. These are basic values that kids learn at a very young age and that we encourage them to apply in all areas of their lives. And in a country where we teach our children that everyone is equal under the law, discriminating against same-sex couples just isn't right. It's as simple as that."<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/2012_Democratic_National_Convention" title="2012 Democratic National Convention">2012 DNC</a> Michelle said, "Barack knows the American Dream because he's lived it&#160;... and he wants everyone in this country to have that same opportunity, no matter who we are, or where we're from, or what we look like, or who we love."<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Domestic_travels">Domestic travels</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Obama_heads_to_Selma_for_50th_anniversary_speech_150307-F-WU507-020.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Obama_heads_to_Selma_for_50th_anniversary_speech_150307-F-WU507-020.jpg/220px-Obama_heads_to_Selma_for_50th_anniversary_speech_150307-F-WU507-020.jpg" width="220" height="253" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Obama_heads_to_Selma_for_50th_anniversary_speech_150307-F-WU507-020.jpg/330px-Obama_heads_to_Selma_for_50th_anniversary_speech_150307-F-WU507-020.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Obama_heads_to_Selma_for_50th_anniversary_speech_150307-F-WU507-020.jpg/440px-Obama_heads_to_Selma_for_50th_anniversary_speech_150307-F-WU507-020.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3374" data-file-height="3886" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Obama_heads_to_Selma_for_50th_anniversary_speech_150307-F-WU507-020.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Malia and Sasha Obama prepare to enter Air Force One, Michelle Obama and President Obama behind them, on March 7, 2015.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In May 2009, Obama delivered the commencement speech at a graduating ceremony at <a href="/wiki/UC_Merced" class="mw-redirect" title="UC Merced">UC Merced</a> in <a href="/wiki/Merced_County,_California" title="Merced County, California">Merced County, California</a>, the address being praised afterward by students who found her relatable. Kevin Fagan of the <i><a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Chronicle" title="San Francisco Chronicle">San Francisco Chronicle</a></i> wrote that there was chemistry between Obama and the students.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2013, Obama attended the 50th anniversary ceremony for the <a href="/wiki/March_on_Washington" class="mw-redirect" title="March on Washington">March on Washington</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_Memorial" title="Lincoln Memorial">Lincoln Memorial</a>. Positive attention was brought to Obama's attire, a black sleeveless dress with red flowers, designed by <a href="/wiki/Tracy_Reese" title="Tracy Reese">Tracy Reese</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> Reese reacted by releasing a public statement that he was honored the First Lady "would choose to wear one of our designs during the celebration of such a deeply significant historical moment".<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barack_and_Michelle_Obama_holding_hands_at_the_event_to_commemorate_the_50th_Anniversary_of_Bloody_Sunday_and_the_Selma_to_Montgomery_civil_rights_marches.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Barack_and_Michelle_Obama_holding_hands_at_the_event_to_commemorate_the_50th_Anniversary_of_Bloody_Sunday_and_the_Selma_to_Montgomery_civil_rights_marches.jpg/220px-Barack_and_Michelle_Obama_holding_hands_at_the_event_to_commemorate_the_50th_Anniversary_of_Bloody_Sunday_and_the_Selma_to_Montgomery_civil_rights_marches.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Barack_and_Michelle_Obama_holding_hands_at_the_event_to_commemorate_the_50th_Anniversary_of_Bloody_Sunday_and_the_Selma_to_Montgomery_civil_rights_marches.jpg/330px-Barack_and_Michelle_Obama_holding_hands_at_the_event_to_commemorate_the_50th_Anniversary_of_Bloody_Sunday_and_the_Selma_to_Montgomery_civil_rights_marches.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Barack_and_Michelle_Obama_holding_hands_at_the_event_to_commemorate_the_50th_Anniversary_of_Bloody_Sunday_and_the_Selma_to_Montgomery_civil_rights_marches.jpg/440px-Barack_and_Michelle_Obama_holding_hands_at_the_event_to_commemorate_the_50th_Anniversary_of_Bloody_Sunday_and_the_Selma_to_Montgomery_civil_rights_marches.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barack_and_Michelle_Obama_holding_hands_at_the_event_to_commemorate_the_50th_Anniversary_of_Bloody_Sunday_and_the_Selma_to_Montgomery_civil_rights_marches.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Michelle Obama and President Obama hold hands during an event commemorating the 50th anniversary of <a href="/wiki/Selma_to_Montgomery_marches#.22Bloody_Sunday.22_events" title="Selma to Montgomery marches">Bloody Sunday</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In March 2015, Obama traveled to <a href="/wiki/Selma,_Alabama" title="Selma, Alabama">Selma, Alabama</a>, with her family to commemorate the fiftieth anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/Selma_to_Montgomery_marches" title="Selma to Montgomery marches">Selma to Montgomery marches</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> After President Obama's remarks there, the Obamas joined original marchers in crossing the <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Pettus_Bridge" title="Edmund Pettus Bridge">Edmund Pettus Bridge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2015, Obama journeyed to <a href="/wiki/Coachella_Valley" title="Coachella Valley">Coachella Valley</a> while coming to Los Angeles for that year's Special Olympics World Games.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2015, Obama was joined by Jill Biden and <a href="/wiki/Prince_Harry" title="Prince Harry">Prince Harry</a> in visiting a military base in <a href="/wiki/Fort_Belvoir,_Virginia" class="mw-redirect" title="Fort Belvoir, Virginia">Fort Belvoir, Virginia</a>, an attempt on the prince's part to raise awareness to programs supporting harmed service members.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> In December 2015, Obama traveled with her husband to <a href="/wiki/San_Bernardino,_California" title="San Bernardino, California">San Bernardino, California</a>, to meet with families of the victims of <a href="/wiki/2015_San_Bernardino_attack" title="2015 San Bernardino attack">a terrorist attack</a> that occurred two weeks earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_trips">Foreign trips</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Michelle_Obama_at_National_Craft_Museum,_Delhi,_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Michelle_Obama_at_National_Craft_Museum%2C_Delhi%2C_2010.jpg/220px-Michelle_Obama_at_National_Craft_Museum%2C_Delhi%2C_2010.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Michelle_Obama_at_National_Craft_Museum%2C_Delhi%2C_2010.jpg/330px-Michelle_Obama_at_National_Craft_Museum%2C_Delhi%2C_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Michelle_Obama_at_National_Craft_Museum%2C_Delhi%2C_2010.jpg/440px-Michelle_Obama_at_National_Craft_Museum%2C_Delhi%2C_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4096" data-file-height="2731" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Michelle_Obama_at_National_Craft_Museum,_Delhi,_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Obama with children in <a href="/wiki/Delhi" title="Delhi">Delhi</a>, November 8, 2010.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On April 1, 2009, Obama met with Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> in <a href="/wiki/Buckingham_Palace" title="Buckingham Palace">Buckingham Palace</a>, Obama embracing her before attending an event with world leaders.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> Obama praised her, though the hug generated controversy for being out of protocol when greeting Elizabeth.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2010, Obama traveled to <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, her first solo visit to a nation.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> In Mexico, Obama spoke to students, encouraging them to take responsibility for their futures.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> Referring to the underprivileged children, Obama argued that "potential can be found in some of the most unlikely places", citing herself and her husband as examples.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup></p>
<p>Obama traveled to Africa for the second official trip in June 2011, touring <a href="/wiki/Johannesburg" title="Johannesburg">Johannesburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Town" title="Cape Town">Cape Town</a> and <a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a> and meeting with <a href="/wiki/Graca_Machel" class="mw-redirect" title="Graca Machel">Graca Machel</a>. Obama was also involved with community events in the foreign countries.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> It was commented by White House staff that her trip to Africa would advance the foreign policy of her husband.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2014, Obama visited China along with her two daughters Malia and Sasha, and her mother Marian Robinson. She met with <a href="/wiki/Peng_Liyuan" title="Peng Liyuan">Peng Liyuan</a>, the wife of Chinese President <a href="/wiki/Xi_Jinping" title="Xi Jinping">Xi Jinping</a>, visited historic and cultural sites, as well as a university and two high schools.<sup id="cite_ref-MichelleChinaVisit_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MichelleChinaVisit-200">[200]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> Deputy National Security Adviser <a href="/wiki/Ben_Rhodes_(White_House_staffer)" title="Ben Rhodes (White House staffer)">Ben Rhodes</a> said that the visit and intent in Obama journeying there was to symbolize "the relationship between the United States and China is not just between leaders, it's a relationship between peoples".<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2015, Obama traveled to <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> alongside her husband, following the death of <a href="/wiki/Abdullah_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="Abdullah of Saudi Arabia">King Abdullah</a>. She received criticism for not covering her head in a nation where women are forbidden from publicly not doing so,<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> though Obama was defended for being a foreigner and thus not having to submit to Saudi Arabia's customs,<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> even being praised in some corners.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> Obama was neither greeted nor acknowledged by King Salman during the encounter.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:President_and_First_Lady_Obama,_With_Saudi_King_Salman,_Shake_Hands_With_Members_of_the_Saudi_Royal_Family.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/President_and_First_Lady_Obama%2C_With_Saudi_King_Salman%2C_Shake_Hands_With_Members_of_the_Saudi_Royal_Family.jpg/220px-President_and_First_Lady_Obama%2C_With_Saudi_King_Salman%2C_Shake_Hands_With_Members_of_the_Saudi_Royal_Family.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/President_and_First_Lady_Obama%2C_With_Saudi_King_Salman%2C_Shake_Hands_With_Members_of_the_Saudi_Royal_Family.jpg/330px-President_and_First_Lady_Obama%2C_With_Saudi_King_Salman%2C_Shake_Hands_With_Members_of_the_Saudi_Royal_Family.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/President_and_First_Lady_Obama%2C_With_Saudi_King_Salman%2C_Shake_Hands_With_Members_of_the_Saudi_Royal_Family.jpg/440px-President_and_First_Lady_Obama%2C_With_Saudi_King_Salman%2C_Shake_Hands_With_Members_of_the_Saudi_Royal_Family.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2768" data-file-height="1841" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:President_and_First_Lady_Obama,_With_Saudi_King_Salman,_Shake_Hands_With_Members_of_the_Saudi_Royal_Family.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Michelle and Barack Obama with <a href="/wiki/King_Salman" class="mw-redirect" title="King Salman">King Salman</a> of <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> and members of the Saudi Royal Family, January 27, 2015.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In June 2015, Obama undertook a weeklong trip to London and three Italian cities. In London, she spoke with students about international education for adolescent girls and met with both British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prince_Harry" title="Prince Harry">Prince Harry</a>. She was joined by her two daughters and mother.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> In November, she spent a week in <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, her first official visit to the Middle East. She continued advancing her initiative for international education for women by speaking at the 2015 World Innovation Summit for Education for the "Let Girls Learn" initiative in <a href="/wiki/Doha,_Qatar" class="mw-redirect" title="Doha, Qatar">Doha, Qatar</a> and touring a school in <a href="/wiki/Amman,_Jordan" class="mw-redirect" title="Amman, Jordan">Amman, Jordan</a>, where she met with female students.<sup id="cite_ref-2015CNN_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015CNN-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> During the Qatar trip, Obama had intended to visit Jordan as well, but the trip was canceled due to weather conditions. In Jordan, Obama had intended to visit an <a href="/wiki/Amman,_Jordan" class="mw-redirect" title="Amman, Jordan">Amman</a> school, which had been constructed with assistance from U.S. funds.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2016, Obama accompanied her husband and children to <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> in a trip that was seen by the administration as having the possibility of positively impacting relations between the country and America.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> Later that month, the First Couple and their daughters traveled to <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> meeting with Argentine President <a href="/wiki/Mauricio_Macri" title="Mauricio Macri">Mauricio Macri</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Midterm_elections">Midterm elections</span></h3>
<p>Obama campaigned for Democratic candidates in the 2010 midterm elections,<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> making her debut on the campaign trail in <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee,_Wisconsin" class="mw-redirect" title="Milwaukee, Wisconsin">Milwaukee, Wisconsin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup> By the time she began campaigning, Obama's approval rating was 20 percentage points higher than her husband.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup> Though Obama indicated in January 2010 that a consensus had not been made about whether she would campaign,<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> speculation of her involvement came from her large approval rating as well as reports that she had been invited to speak at events with Democrats such as <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Boxer" title="Barbara Boxer">Barbara Boxer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mary_Jo_Kilroy" title="Mary Jo Kilroy">Mary Jo Kilroy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joe_Sestak" title="Joe Sestak">Joe Sestak</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup> She toured seven states in two weeks within October 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> Though viewed as essential by the White House, aides reported that she would not become deeply involved with political discussions nor engage Republicans in public disputes.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup> After the elections took place, only six of the thirteen Democratic candidates Obama had campaigned for won. The <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> concluded that while Obama was indeed more popular than her husband, her "election scorecard proved no better than his, particularly in her home state."<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Michelle_Obama_at_SNHU_October_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Michelle_Obama_at_SNHU_October_2016.jpg/220px-Michelle_Obama_at_SNHU_October_2016.jpg" width="220" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Michelle_Obama_at_SNHU_October_2016.jpg/330px-Michelle_Obama_at_SNHU_October_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Michelle_Obama_at_SNHU_October_2016.jpg/440px-Michelle_Obama_at_SNHU_October_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3102" data-file-height="2899" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Michelle_Obama_at_SNHU_October_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Obama speaks at a <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton_presidential_campaign,_2016" title="Hillary Clinton presidential campaign, 2016">Hillary Clinton presidential campaign</a> rally at <a href="/wiki/Southern_New_Hampshire_University" title="Southern New Hampshire University">Southern New Hampshire University</a>, October 13, 2016.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Obama was a participant in the 2014 midterm elections, held at a time where her popularity superseded her husband's to such an extent that it was theorized that she would receive a much larger outpour of support in campaigning. Reporting her travel to <a href="/wiki/Denver,_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="Denver, Colorado">Denver, Colorado</a>, David Lightman wrote that while Democrats did not want President Obama to campaign for them, "the first lady is very popular".<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> In May 2014, Obama was found to have a 61% favorable approval rating from a CNN poll, her husband coming in at 43%.<sup id="cite_ref-2014CNN_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014CNN-228">[228]</a></sup> In a video released in July, as part of an effort to encourage <a href="/wiki/Voter_turnout" title="Voter turnout">voter turnout</a>, she called on voters to be "hungry as you were back in 2008 and 2012".<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> Obama appeared at a fundraiser in Georgia in September for Democratic senate candidate <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Nunn" title="Michelle Nunn">Michelle Nunn</a>. Obama's approach to campaigning in Georgia strayed from discussing current events and instead broadly stressed the importance of registering to vote and turning out during the elections.<sup id="cite_ref-2014CNN_228-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014CNN-228">[228]</a></sup> Obama's infrequent appearances came from her dislike of being away from her children and Washington politics as well as her distaste for the opposition by Republicans to her husband's agenda and her view that Democrats in the U.S. Senate had not sufficiently been supporters of her initiatives to end childhood obesity.<sup id="cite_ref-2014NYT_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014NYT-231">[231]</a></sup> Obama raised her profile in October,<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup> touring three states in four days.<sup id="cite_ref-2014NYT_231-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014NYT-231">[231]</a></sup> Obama called the elections her husband's "last campaign".<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hillary_Clinton_2016_presidential_campaign">Hillary Clinton 2016 presidential campaign</span></h3>
<p>Obama endorsed Democratic nominee Hillary Clinton and made several high-profile speeches in favor of her, including an address at the <a href="/wiki/2016_Democratic_National_Convention" title="2016 Democratic National Convention">2016 Democratic National Convention</a>. She also appeared multiple times on the campaign trail in either solo or joint appearances with Clinton.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup> On October 13, 2016, Obama heavily criticized Republican presidential nominee <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> for the statements he made in a <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump_and_Billy_Bush_recording_controversy" class="mw-redirect" title="Donald Trump and Billy Bush recording controversy">2005 audio recording</a> while at a Clinton rally in <a href="/wiki/Manchester,_New_Hampshire" title="Manchester, New Hampshire">Manchester, New Hampshire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup> A week later, Trump attempted to revive past comments Obama made in regards to Clinton during the 2008 presidential election.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_image_and_style">Public image and style</span></h3>
<p>With the ascent of her husband as a prominent national politician, Obama has become a part of popular culture. In May 2006, <i><a href="/wiki/Essence_(magazine)" title="Essence (magazine)">Essence</a></i> listed her among "25 of the World's Most Inspiring Women."<sup id="cite_ref-biogtv_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biogtv-240">[240]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FLS_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLS-241">[241]</a></sup> In July 2007, <i><a href="/wiki/Vanity_Fair_(magazine)" title="Vanity Fair (magazine)">Vanity Fair</a></i> listed her among "10 of the World's Best Dressed People." She was an honorary guest at <a href="/wiki/Oprah_Winfrey%27s_Legends_Ball" title="Oprah Winfrey's Legends Ball">Oprah Winfrey's Legends Ball</a> as a "young'un" paying tribute to the 'Legends,' who helped pave the way for African American women. In September 2007, <i><a href="/wiki/02138" title="02138">02138</a></i> magazine listed her 58th of 'The Harvard 100'; a list of the prior year's most influential <a href="/wiki/Category:Harvard_University_alumni" title="Category:Harvard University alumni">Harvard alumni</a>. Her husband was ranked fourth.<sup id="cite_ref-biogtv_240-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biogtv-240">[240]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Top100_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top100-242">[242]</a></sup> In July 2008, she made a repeat appearance on the <i>Vanity Fair</i> international best dressed list.<sup id="cite_ref-MOmraotVFibdl_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOmraotVFibdl-243">[243]</a></sup> She also appeared on the 2008 <i><a href="/wiki/People_(magazine)" title="People (magazine)">People</a></i> list of best-dressed women and was praised by the magazine for her "classic and confident" look.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:184px;max-width:184px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Obamas_walk_down_PA_Ave._1-20-09_hires_090120-N-0696M-546a.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Barack and Michelle Obama hold hands and smile while walking; she waves to a crowd. She wears a gold embroidered dress and coat; he wears a black overcoat and burgundy scarf. A serious man in a dark suit watches nearby." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Obamas_walk_down_PA_Ave._1-20-09_hires_090120-N-0696M-546a.jpg/180px-Obamas_walk_down_PA_Ave._1-20-09_hires_090120-N-0696M-546a.jpg" width="180" height="129" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Obamas_walk_down_PA_Ave._1-20-09_hires_090120-N-0696M-546a.jpg/270px-Obamas_walk_down_PA_Ave._1-20-09_hires_090120-N-0696M-546a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Obamas_walk_down_PA_Ave._1-20-09_hires_090120-N-0696M-546a.jpg/360px-Obamas_walk_down_PA_Ave._1-20-09_hires_090120-N-0696M-546a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2358" data-file-height="1692" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Michelle Obama wore <a href="/wiki/Isabel_Toledo" title="Isabel Toledo">Isabel Toledo</a> clothes made of <a href="/wiki/St._Gallen_Embroidery" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Gallen Embroidery">St.&#160;Gallen Embroidery</a> to the <a href="/wiki/First_inauguration_of_Barack_Obama" title="First inauguration of Barack Obama">2009 presidential inauguration</a>.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Barack_and_Michelle_Obama_at_the_Home_States_Ball.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Barack and Michelle Obama dance arm-in-arm and smile. She wears a white dress, large ring, long earrings and a bracelet. He wears a black tuxedo." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Barack_and_Michelle_Obama_at_the_Home_States_Ball.jpg/180px-Barack_and_Michelle_Obama_at_the_Home_States_Ball.jpg" width="180" height="189" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Barack_and_Michelle_Obama_at_the_Home_States_Ball.jpg/270px-Barack_and_Michelle_Obama_at_the_Home_States_Ball.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Barack_and_Michelle_Obama_at_the_Home_States_Ball.jpg/360px-Barack_and_Michelle_Obama_at_the_Home_States_Ball.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1467" data-file-height="1542" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The Obamas dance at a presidential inaugural ball.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the time of her husband's election, some sources anticipated that as a high-profile <a href="/wiki/African_American" class="mw-redirect" title="African American">African-American</a> woman in a stable marriage Obama would be a positive role model who would influence the view the world has of African-Americans.<sup id="cite_ref-WMMtU_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WMMtU-246">[246]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup> Her fashion choices were part of the 2009 <a href="/wiki/Fashion_week" title="Fashion week">Fashion week</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup> but Obama's influence in the field did not have the impact on the paucity of African-American models who participate, that some thought it might.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup></p>
<p>Obama's public support grew in her early months as First Lady,<sup id="cite_ref-MIFOTS_134-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MIFOTS-134">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MR_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MR-251">[251]</a></sup> as she was accepted as a <a href="/wiki/Role_model" title="Role model">role model</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MIFOTS_134-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MIFOTS-134">[134]</a></sup> On her first trip abroad in April 2009, she toured a cancer ward with <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Jane_Brown" title="Sarah Jane Brown">Sarah Brown</a>, wife of British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Brown" title="Gordon Brown">Gordon Brown</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i> described her first trip abroad as an exhibition of her so-called "star power"<sup id="cite_ref-MR_251-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MR-251">[251]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/MSN" title="MSN">MSN</a> described it as a display of sartorial elegance.<sup id="cite_ref-FLS_241-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLS-241">[241]</a></sup> Questions were raised by some in the American and British media regarding <a href="/wiki/Protocol_(diplomacy)" title="Protocol (diplomacy)">protocol</a> when the Obamas met <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a><sup id="cite_ref-TQaMO_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TQaMO-253">[253]</a></sup> and Michelle reciprocated a touch on her back by the Queen during a reception, purportedly against traditional royal etiquette.<sup id="cite_ref-TQaMO_253-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TQaMO-253">[253]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup> Palace sources denied that any breach in etiquette had occurred.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup></p>
<p>Obama has been compared to <a href="/wiki/Jacqueline_Kennedy_Onassis" title="Jacqueline Kennedy Onassis">Jacqueline Kennedy</a> due to her sense of style,<sup id="cite_ref-MOmraotVFibdl_243-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOmraotVFibdl-243">[243]</a></sup> and also to <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Bush" title="Barbara Bush">Barbara Bush</a> for her discipline and decorum.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup> Obama's style has been described as "fashion populist."<sup id="cite_ref-VLiCBTO_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VLiCBTO-50">[50]</a></sup> In 2010, she wore clothes, many high end, from more than 50 design companies with less expensive pieces from <a href="/wiki/J.Crew" title="J.Crew">J.Crew</a> and <a href="/wiki/Target_Corporation" title="Target Corporation">Target</a>, and the same year a study found that her patronage was worth an average of $14&#160;million to a company.<sup id="cite_ref-Horyn_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Horyn-258">[258]</a></sup> She became a fashion trendsetter, in particular favoring sleeveless dresses, including her first-term official portrait in a dress by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Kors" title="Michael Kors">Michael Kors</a>, and her ball gowns designed by <a href="/wiki/Jason_Wu" title="Jason Wu">Jason Wu</a> for both inaugurals.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">[259]</a></sup> She has also been known for wearing clothes by African designers such as <a href="/wiki/Mimi_Plange" title="Mimi Plange">Mimi Plange</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duro_Olowu" title="Duro Olowu">Duro Olowu</a>,&#160;Maki Oh, and&#160;Osei Duro,&#160;and styles such as the <a href="/wiki/Adire_(textile_art)" title="Adire (textile art)">Adire</a> fabric.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">[260]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">[261]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup></p>
<p>Obama appeared on the cover and in a photo spread in the March 2009 issue of <i><a href="/wiki/Vogue_(magazine)" title="Vogue (magazine)">Vogue</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-MOgcoVm_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOgcoVm-263">[263]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MOmVc_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOmVc-264">[264]</a></sup> Every First Lady since <a href="/wiki/Lou_Henry_Hoover" title="Lou Henry Hoover">Lou Hoover</a> (except <a href="/wiki/Bess_Truman" title="Bess Truman">Bess Truman</a>) has been in <i>Vogue</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-MOgcoVm_263-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOgcoVm-263">[263]</a></sup> but only Hillary Clinton had previously appeared on the cover.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup> Obama later appeared two more times on the cover of <i>Vogue</i>, while First Lady, the last time in December 2016, with photographs by <a href="/wiki/Annie_Leibovitz" title="Annie Leibovitz">Annie Leibovitz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup> In August 2011, she became the first woman ever to appear on the cover of <i><a href="/wiki/Better_Homes_and_Gardens_(magazine)" title="Better Homes and Gardens (magazine)">Better Homes and Gardens</a></i> magazine, and the first person in 48 years.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/85th_Academy_Awards" title="85th Academy Awards">2013 Academy Awards</a>, she became the first <a href="/wiki/First_Lady" title="First Lady">First Lady</a> to announce the winner of an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Oscar</a> (Best Picture which went to <i><a href="/wiki/Argo_(2012_film)" title="Argo (2012 film)">Argo</a></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup></p>
<p>The media have been criticized for focusing more on the <a href="/wiki/First_Lady" title="First Lady">First Lady</a>'s fashion sense than her serious contributions.<sup id="cite_ref-VLiCBTO_50-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VLiCBTO-50">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup> She said after the 2008 election that she would like to focus attention as First Lady on issues of concern to military and working families.<sup id="cite_ref-WMMtU_246-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WMMtU-246">[246]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">[270]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup> In 2008 <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> blogger, <a href="/wiki/PBS" title="PBS">PBS</a> host and <a href="/wiki/E._W._Scripps_Company" title="E. W. Scripps Company">Scripps Howard</a> columnist <a href="/wiki/Bonnie_Erb%C3%A9" title="Bonnie Erbé">Bonnie Erbé</a> argued that Obama's own publicists seemed to be feeding the emphasis on style over substance,<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup> and has stated that Obama is miscasting herself by overemphasizing style.<sup id="cite_ref-MOSWW_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MOSWW-73">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Subsequent_activities">Subsequent activities</span></h2>
<p>In May 2017, during an appearance at the Partnership for a Healthier America conference, Obama rebuked the Trump administration for its delay of a federal requirement designed to increase the nutritional standards for school lunches.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup> In June, while attending the WWDC in <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="Silicon Valley, California">Silicon Valley, California</a>, Obama called for tech companies to add women for the diversifying of their ranks.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup> In July, Obama honored <a href="/wiki/Eunice_Shriver" class="mw-redirect" title="Eunice Shriver">Eunice Shriver</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2017_ESPY_Awards" title="2017 ESPY Awards">2017 ESPY Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup> In September, Obama delivered an address at the tech conference in Utah charging the Trump administration with having a fearful White House,<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">[277]</a></sup> appeared in a video for the Global Citizens Festival advocating more attention to giving young girls an education,<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup> and attended the Inbound 2017 conference in Boston.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">[279]</a></sup></p>

<li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-6">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20110927083448/http://www.islandpacket.com/2009/04/04/804596/examining-michelle-obamas-lowcountry.html">"Examining Michelle Obama's Lowcountry roots"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Island_Packet" title="The Island Packet">The Island Packet</a></i>.
